Spring and Autumn

On Reading the Classics 211

— Nineteen

Recently, enlightened people, seeing the prevalence of heresy, want to add a classics reading course in schools to correct the morals of the present decadent society and to rectify people's hearts. This is indeed right. The words of the sages are like the sun and moon traversing the sky and the rivers flowing on the earth. Since the Han Dynasty, which scholar could escape the study of the classics if they wanted to gain an official position? The Han Dynasty established professors of the Five Classics, and the Song Dynasty used the meaning of the classics to select scholars. During that time, many famous officials and great Confucians emerged. Those who want to make a living by writing know this. Therefore, although some people regard reading the classics as reversing the times, I ultimately believe that it is beyond reproach.

However, when it comes to the classics, quantitatively speaking, according to Duan Yucai's definition, there are as many as twenty-one kinds. Young students have many courses and little time, so it is difficult to read them one by one. Qualitatively speaking, Yan Ruoqu spent twenty or thirty years of textual research to determine that the Book of Documents was a forgery. This shows that "exhaustively studying the classics" is also very difficult.

If we talk about selective reading, it is indeed feasible, but I believe that the selection of materials is also highly debatable. I offer my humble opinion as follows:

(1) Those that run counter to the trend of the times should not be selected. "The people can be made to follow it, but not to know it" is inconsistent with "democracy." "Men should be in their proper position outside, and women should be in their proper position inside" is also incompatible with the principle of "equality between men and women."

"Do not enter a dangerous country, do not live in a chaotic country" encourages people to take a passive attitude towards national affairs. All of these should not be selected as teaching materials.

(2) Those involving love and sexuality should not be selected. "Climbing over the wall of the eastern neighbor to seduce his daughter; seducing her can lead to marriage, not seducing her will not lead to marriage" and the chapter on the people of Qi having one wife and one concubine are both wonderful passages by Mencius, but they should not be selected. Zhang Sheng jumping over the pink wall is due to the poison of the former; the rich keeping concubines is due to the demon of the latter. Furthermore, the Book of Songs, it seems that everyone now knows that most of the odes of the fifteen states are folk love songs. In fact, this saying "has existed since ancient times." Huang Chaoying of the Song Dynasty mentioned this in his "Xiang Su Ji" long ago, but it has only become popular recently. If you select the odes of the states as teaching materials, how is it different from selecting the tune of "Sister, I love you"? Isn't it the same as teaching lewdness? The "male and female essences combine, and all things are created" in the Book of Changes should not be selected as teaching materials. If students want to study the "essence combination" problem, how will the teacher deal with it? Moreover, modern education emphasizes interest the most. If the teacher fully explains the meaning of this sentence, he will become Zhang Boshu II. Conversely, if he pretends not to know or speaks vaguely, the students will say, "You don't even understand this." As for the things like "Duke Xuan of Wei committing incest with a barbarian concubine" in Zuo Zhuan, it is even more out of the question and should not be selected as teaching materials to avoid harming the descendants of generations of noble families.

The above is what I consider dangerous, and I dare not remain silent. Is it appropriate? I dare to ask the enlightened people who advocate reading the classics.

Bridge 212

— Broken Cauldron

Many children are swimming under the bridge, swimming, swimming past, and swimming back. Some are standing, holding checkered earth cloth towels, wiping their bodies for a while, but then squeezing back into the water! Some are chasing and fighting, like frogs, splashing water, laughing, and shouting.

Several children are standing on the bridge, watching, laughing, and shouting along. Some adults are sitting on the stone bridge railings, waving palm-leaf fans, chatting idly. Suddenly, "plop," there is a sound, and another naked child somersaults into the water. It takes a long time before he shows his head.

There is a cattle herder, holding the cow with one hand and a pair of cloth shoes in the other. He runs over, humming a little tune. Watching, he ties the cow to the willow tree by the river. He rolls up the legs of his trousers, puts his shoes on the ground beside him, sits under the willow tree, and washes his feet, "splash, splash." A storyteller, beating a long drum and a gong, holding the stick in his hand, kissing the stone ground, "da-da-da," he comes over, followed by a crowd of people. He steps onto the bridgehead and sits on the railing: "dong-dong-tui, dong-dong-tui, tui-tui-tui-tui, dong-dong-tui," beating, beating.

"Hey, storyteller! How much to sing 'Liang Shanbo and Zhu Yingtai'?" someone asks.

"Six dimes. I'm used to singing it, no bargaining."

"Well, it's six dimes. Six dimes is public money. Children don't count. There are sixteen people here, so six dimes is one hundred and forty-four copper coins. Six nines are fifty-four, one nine is nine, one hundred and forty-four copper coins. Everyone takes out nine copper coins!" another says.

The long drum and gong start beating again! The storyteller opens his husk-like throat and sings: "Speaking news, telling news, news happened in..."

Son 213

— Virtuous Virtuous

"At thirty, no son is a mediocre life; at forty, no son is a lonely life; at fifty, no son is unrespected; at sixty, no son is as bitter as Coptis chinensis." Sons are generally sweet. "Having wealth without a son is not considered rich; having a son without wealth is not considered poor." So sons are like the first prize of the aviation highway lottery, worth 500,000.

Guanyin Bodhisattva knows how to grant sons, and the Earth God also knows how to grant sons. No wonder the news of "one birth of three children" is often printed on posters and sold. Originally, as long as you are "sincere, you will be effective," what do you have to fear? You will "seek a son and get a son," "every request will be answered." No wonder China's population has changed from 400 million to 470 million in one fell swoop. Poor men "with sons but no wealth" are dragging a group of snotty big sons and scabby-headed little sons. Each of them is a rich man, I must apologize for my disrespect. I can't get pregnant, even after marrying five or six concubines. For eight or ten years, I can't even break wind, let alone have a fat-headed, big-eared son. Every year, I go to India to offer incense, pray to gods and worship Buddhas, repair myself externally and internally, and eat seed elixirs as food, but it's still the same. Seeing that such a big fortune will belong to others when I kick the bucket, how can I not be anxious? But what if I have a son? Won't I still see King Yama empty-handed?

"Foolish parents have always been many, but who has seen filial grandchildren?"

Since Adam and Eve until now, there has been no breaking of the new record of "Twenty-Four Filial Exemplars." Those who commit crimes and "bring disaster to their illustrious fathers" are "readily available," but those who are "unconscious of suffering" cannot be found even with a lantern. "The old master is dead." "Let me finish my sixteenth game of mahjong." Okay, think about it. A son, this is also a son sent by Guanyin Bodhisattva and the Earth God.

After saying so much bad things about sons, everyone is afraid of being scared by sons, right? Don't be afraid. Having a son is like winning the lottery. Although the first prize is 500,000, it is not guaranteed, but at the moment when the "prize is about to be announced," the tip of the tongue and the space between the teeth are always sweet, and that is enough. "Raising a son to guard against old age" still seems unbreakable.

Casual Talk on Cartoons 214

— Written by Qian Yun, Drawn by Dong Liang

Contradictory Reality

How majestic was Coachman A-da! Nothing special, it was when he started singing the Five Watches and Ten Farewells and crying for the Seventh Seventh, even though he read many wrong words, it was enough to attract a dozen comrades to surround him and worship him.

When he was free, he would mop the floor in his master's study. He then lamented and thought: This is because his master knows more words and can work at a desk and ride in a car. Because I know fewer words, I dare to be downgraded to the floor and pull a cart. Friend A-er, if you can read "Yang Yanhui Sits in the Palace Courtyard, Thinking to Himself..." hasn't he changed to sitting on a soft cushion in a car? So he is not like me, earning only ten yuan a month!

His thinking is not wrong, because there is no big boss in the study who is illiterate. But there are also contradictions, for example, among the tens of millions of unemployed people in Shanghai, there are many college students and students who have studied abroad. It is difficult to find something like A-da's salary! If they really went to pull a cart, they wouldn't have the strength.

Of course, this is not advocating not to study. It's just that the way out after studying has really become a problem! If I have a son (it's better not to have a son), I will definitely ask him to work and study from a young age. This part-time job, whether it's picking up trash on the road or enduring the hardships of the wind and frost, is to avoid not being able to find food in the future. If I don't write, I can do something like a coachman. The reason: I don't have an inheritance!

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 215

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 12: Poor and Humble Join the Army, Sickly Husband Falls Behind; Sacrifice is Sweet to Resign, Soldiers are Affectionate

This soldier is called Yu Shouzheng. He is someone who graduated from high school and is the most clever in the platoon. Sheng Shimin had not been a soldier for long and thought this was very reasonable. So, starting with the platoon leader, one person went to the merchant, another person went to the merchant, and another person went to the merchant until they reached the battalion commander. This battalion commander didn't want the "embroidery ball wind" to happen in his battalion. Since he wanted to ask for sick leave to go out, he let him go and approved his departure. Zhao Ziqiang couldn't go out for the past two days and was worried because he didn't know what to do, write a letter back, not knowing what the real situation was, so he didn't know what to say in the letter. Now that Sheng Shimin was going out, he could use his words to report the news back. So he gave Sheng Shimin a dollar and told him some words, asking him to see his old master. Sheng Shimin felt that this company commander was too good, and he left the camp with many thanks. He hired a car at the camp gate and went straight to the Zhao family in Haidian. When he arrived at the Zhao family's gate, the dense goose feather snowflakes kept pouring down. Sometimes, a gust of wind blew in the snow, rolling up the branches and dancing a Hu Xuan, rushing straight at people. Sheng Shimin was a sick person and couldn't withstand this kind of severe cold. Getting out of the car, entering the Zhao family's gate, he squatted on the ground and hummed twice. Gui Zhi was moving the coal balls on the ground in the courtyard into the house with a basket, looking up at the sky. The sky was also making things difficult for the poor, snowing so heavily on this day. She suddenly heard a humming sound and was startled. She immediately ran out and looked at the door to see what was going on. She saw Sheng Shimin squatting on the ground with a pale face and couldn't help but take two steps back, holding the wall and looking at him, saying: What are you doing? (143)

Children's Mian Yuan

Education of the Hand 216

— Jie Lu

Although people's knowledge and skills all come through... but the eyes are the "gate of knowledge" and the ears are the "palace of learning." Those with nimble ears are called "smart," and those with nimble eyes are called "bright." Those who see and hear a lot are smart people. The biggest drawback of modern education is that it doesn't regulate the use of the brain and the use of force. There are too many subjects and too many books, so young students often develop myopia, tinnitus, and neurasthenia. Children's bodies and minds have not yet fully developed. What I have always advocated is to impart knowledge through work, and I am strongly opposed to injection-style education. Therefore, I have this contribution on "Education of the Hand":

Try looking at how deaf-mutes study. Don't they rely on their hands? There is still hope for blindness, as long as the hand's instinct doesn't disappear. Today, people only know that intelligence is poured in through the ears and eyes, ignoring the "education of the hand." This is a big shortcoming! The hand is a useful tool for people. It can train the body, create things, and represent meanings. It is really more useful than the ears and eyes. How is it called training the body? Such as driving horses, rowing boats, swinging, playing table tennis, doing Tai Chi, and various exercises, not only can maintain health, but also can promote health. Lively children, come and use your hands to train your bodies! How is it called creating things? It's a long story, but aren't all the things we use in our lives made by hand? We still have to use these hands to create all kinds of new things. For example, the hand can count. The thumb counts as five, the index finger counts as six, the middle finger counts as seven, the ring finger counts as eight, and the little finger counts as nine. Both hands are the same. As long as you bring your fingers together, you can calculate multiplication. For example, six times seven, put the right hand's index finger against the left hand's middle finger. Add the fingers above, which is three, making it the tens place, which is thirty. The fingers below the right hand are four fingers, multiplied by three fingers on the left hand, equals twelve; thirty plus twelve, equals forty-two, which is the product of six times seven. The rest can be inferred. Fingers can also be used to calculate the size of the months of the Gregorian calendar. The method is to count on the knuckles of the fist. The raised ones are big months (thirty-one days), and the recessed ones are small months (thirty days). Count in order, and you won't make a mistake. The only exception is February 28th in a common year and 29th in a leap year. The hand can also project various shapes such as squirrels, sheep, rabbits, dogs, monks, and Taoists in the light, which children like to play with. You can also tie the fingers together to form many names. How is it called representing meaning? We know that there is "flag language" in the Boy Scouts, which can represent speech. The hand also has this wonderful use. When children are kicking shuttlecocks and playing with balls, they often turn the little hands and palms over and over again to represent picking, doesn't this resemble raising a hand to represent meaning during a meeting? Buying and selling and prices in the stock exchange are all represented by hand, so we know that the hand can indeed represent meaning.

Mantis and Ant 217

— Zhou Zheng

The majestic sun emitted thousands of fiery rays, ironing everything on the earth as if with an iron.

Only the ants, among the lower insects, were still diligently seeking what they needed in the scorching light. Their feet were scalded; their heads were hot; and their two clever antennae, bumping east and west, also showed a very busy expression.

The mantis, with its strong body and arrogant self-importance, walked forward with an air of confidence.

"Great! With such a great body, who am I afraid of?

Who dares to bully me? As long as I press with my arms, they will die! Hmph, no one can compare to me. I'm so happy! Now I'm very tired, let me take a nap." A mantis, gloating and talking to itself, found a cool place and unknowingly went to dreamland.

It bit hard on the mantis's foot with its sharp teeth, wanting to carry it home. How could a small ant drag such a large mantis?

The ant jumped up quickly, rushing back to report the victory. Its brothers and sisters at home were overjoyed at this good news. They were very much like those who had received military education. They lined up neatly and went hurriedly.

One ant bit the mantis's foot, one ant bit the mantis's head, one ant bit the mantis's stomach...

At this time, the mantis woke up and felt a pain and itch all over its body, which was very uncomfortable. It waved its arms wildly, striking at the ants. Although it knocked back a few, the combined strength was so strong that no one could overcome it. The ants fearlessly charged up and bit the mantis.

In the end, did the arrogant mantis finally realize it?

Free Talk

University Education 218

— Yu Dafu

In China today, some people advocate that university education is not necessary. Still others argue that the facade of university education must be maintained, otherwise it will not be possible to obtain the Boxer Indemnity funds, but the liberal arts departments are not necessary, or at most, only one or two universities need to be retained to maintain the facade, and the rest are not necessary.

Those who advocate that university education is not necessary say: "What learning does China need? Throughout the country, is there anyone or anything that can prove that they respect learning? Specialists, excellent scholars who graduate from famous universities at home and abroad, some starve to death, some barely make a living by obtaining an official position, and abandon their entire profession. What genuine talent and practical knowledge does China ultimately need?"

Those who advocate not having liberal arts departments but keeping a few universities to maintain the facade say: "The purpose of studying is to become an official. But why does becoming an official in China necessarily require someone from the liberal arts? Look at us! Those who study civil engineering, mining, geology, and applied chemistry, haven't we all become officials here in the same way? Why do we need liberal arts? In turn, it creates many people who only have fantasies and are out of touch with reality, who speak out against authority and plot against the country, which is detrimental to the country. To maintain the facade and obtain foreign funds, it is enough to have a few universities of science and engineering or scientific research institutes."

Both sides have a point, and the actual situation is indeed the case. Just look at those who are issuing orders and serving the party and the country in China today, aren't they all people who have received university education? However, here I have a small question. I think it is true that learning should be applied, but the cultivation of personality is of course an important function of education. Those who can uphold their beliefs, willingly starve to death, and disdain to conform to the world and flatter others, can justifiably prove the victory of education. There is only a shortage of universities that can cultivate these talents, and there is no reason why they are not necessary. Secondly, even from the perspective of "learning to be applied," is it really the only purpose of studying to become an official? Distributing China's entire population, are there too many liberal arts graduates? Not to mention remote and desolate areas, even in towns and cities slightly farther from the metropolis, how many liberal arts graduates with clear minds are there who handle affairs and guide the masses? The reason why illiterate local bullies and unscrupulous gentry and slightly capable litigious and scoundrels run rampant is because university education is not universal and thorough enough! If we say that university education is not necessary, then educational administrative organs and many other nominal and exploitative organizations that only know how to collect money from the people can be dispensed with first. Is the purpose of university education really just to become an official and cheat money?

The "Usefulness" and "Uselessness" of Literature 219

— Another Realm

The root of the so-called "literature is useless" argument probably lies in a few words from Mr. Ye Shengtao's "Wartime Notes." Mr. Ye said:

"If you say to write propaganda, the propaganda power of the soldiers' own actions is a thousand times stronger than words. If you say to create artistic works that express the spirit of resistance, China is a country where a book selling 10,000 copies is considered a very impressive sales figure. On this point, I think those who hold pens should decline."

This is equivalent to Mr. Zhuan Donghua advising people not to take the path of studying literature in his article "This Road is Impassable" (see the New Year Special Issue of Reading Magazine). These are all words "filled with emotion." If someone rashly thinks that Mr. Ye and Mr. Zhuan are "believers in the uselessness of literature" because of this, it is actually extremely wrong. Mr. Ye is working hard to create, and Mr. Zhuan is busy compiling "Literature" because literature is useful.

Therefore, this is not like what Mr. Qi Fan said, "Half of it is the complaint of frustrated idealists, and the other half is a misunderstanding of the nature of learning..." The important thing is that we should distinguish clearly between the essential effectiveness of literature and the effectiveness of literature in real life. Speaking of the former, who can deny the effectiveness of literature's permanent service to society? When it comes to the latter, various realities are placed before us: among the few percent of readers in China, most are still reading masturbatory novels cast from a triangular house, the manuscript fees are so low that they are almost the same as the price of the paper, university graduates are competing with normal school students for jobs, except for literature for studying abroad, the Ministry of Education has ordered the suspension of liberal arts majors, and people in society evaluate those who study literature as "having no expertise," so the only way out for literary people is the "trembling two golden flowers on both sides!" praised by Zhu Maichen to his divorced wife.

With these facts in front of us, a feeling that literature is useless will naturally arise in our minds, unless they are "successful idealists" who have built foreign houses.

However, this does not hinder the recognition of the essence of literature, and the useful value of literature will not disappear with the Ministry of Education's ban on recruiting liberal arts students.

From "Push" to "Take" 220

— Sun Yang

I heard that there used to be a kind of boxer who had a special massage technique called "tuina" (push and grasp). If someone suffered from a disease like neurasthenia and was as thin as a bamboo pole, they would become as fat as a Buddha after being "tuina"ed for a year or so. Although there is no way to know if this is true or false, it is enough to prove that the ancients also paid attention to "push" and "grasp."

These past couple days, I've seen "Free Talk" discuss "push," and I can't help but feel something. The ancients' "push" seemed to be to activate other people's blood. Today's "push" seems to activate one's own blood. Although the activation of blood is the same, the person being activated is different. In these times, everyone frowns more than smiles. It is difficult for "third-person" to be an exception. Inevitably, sometimes blood rushes to the head. In order to activate one's blood, disregarding the fact that "confused people can't see their enemies clearly," they start "pushing" and "promoting" in a big way. The work of "pushing" is naturally sped up.

When pushing until covered in sweat and breathing heavily, one must first "take." Actually, it doesn't matter if one "takes" first. As Feng Sheng said, the procedure for "pushing" someone who can't afford a boat ticket is to "take" their belongings first. But from what I think, there are many who "push" before "taking." For example, there is often a kind of coachman at the wharf. After you agree to go to a certain place in the British Concession with him, he will carry your luggage onto the carriage and "push" both people and goods to a small inn on Avenue Foch. Then there are young scions with shiny hair, who will present a bill: room fee, carriage fee, wharf fee, tips, and you have to "take" out at least ten dollars. The coachman naturally gets a share. However, the root of the matter is that they "take" more for others and "take" less for themselves. Muddled and confused, they can't recognize their enemies.

Originally, there was nothing wrong with "pushing," but thinking about it afterwards, while you were "pushing" so hard that smoke was coming out of your head, other people were calmly preparing to "take." It's hard not to be ashamed when your enemies are clearly seen!

Trivial Notes on Reading 221

— Xiaoxue

Reading the recently published "Short Letters of Zhou Zuoren" is like being in the deep mountains amidst ice and snow, giving one a sense of "no thought, no action, all worldly ties severed." It's as if one is reading the "Miscellaneous Letters" of the Wei and Jin dynasties, or admiring the "Short Notes" of Su Dongpo and Huang Tingjian. To call it "modern classical prose," I think nothing could be more fitting.

In his first letter to Yu Pingbo, Zhou Zuoren discussed modern essays and sketches, saying:

"I often say that the essays and sketches of today are not new products since the May Fourth Movement, but are actually 'anciently existing,' only now re-emerging. The small essays of today and the works of the Song and Ming dynasties may be somewhat different in style, but the flavor is actually consistent, or perhaps a little Western influence has been added, giving it a new atmosphere."

This kind of judgment, as an explanation of the superficial phenomenon of the "escapist" essays and sketches of the author's school, I think is very interesting. Zhou Zuoren's short letters are such a product. But what can truly be called modern essays and sketches, things that resonate with the pulse of modern social life, will never be like this.

Let's talk about life. In Zhou Zuoren's short letters, what kind of life is written about in the so-called "fragmentary words"? From beginning to end, what is unfolded is nothing more than the following scene:

Reading ancient books, looking at peanuts, inquiring about illness, "Lotus White Wine," "eating blessing tea," idle travel, idle lying, leisure, inviting people for casual chats, writing楹聯, buying books, archaeology, printing ancient-style envelopes and stationery, engraving seals, talking about印泥, talking about dreams, banquets, inviting monks to chant sutras, collecting stamps, carving woodblock books, sitting under the rustling south window.

What he does is completely the life of "ancient hermits," completely isolated from the intense "modern" life. If you also remove the "brandy," "movies," "soda," "beer," "curry rice," "telephone," "proletarian literature," "Don Quixote," "Saturday," "week," "airmail," and a dozen other new terms from the letters, these slight traces of modern life, then, to make a joke, one would not know if it were a posthumous work of Luo Guanzhong or a lost manuscript of Shi Nai'an.

"The more evil the world, the more one turns to leisure" (Letter 32 to Pingbo). How can a person living like this – sitting in "Bitter Rain Studio," "Medicine Cottage," "Bitter Tea Hermitage," playing with seals of the "lotus eater" type, "writing manuscripts to earn a little money for wine" – not be "out of step with body and mind" (the author's words)? "Writing essays is a way to nourish the spirit" (Letter 9 to Fei Ming). The author's understanding is such, so it is no wonder that readers cannot see any images of social life through his personal life.

The author says (Letter 8 to Pingbo):

"A person's attitude towards life is constantly changing, how can one maintain it for thirteen or fourteen years? I, your unworthy servant, examine myself and find that my thoughts have become increasingly decadent, how can I still have the impetuous and aggressive spirit of the May Fourth period?"

From being a warrior in the May Fourth period, gradually turning one's life completely away from "reality," and calling one's most glorious period "impetuous and aggressive," this is of course one of the inevitable tendencies of the result of the conflict between the individual and society, there is nothing strange about it; but, here, readers can also see how cruelly the wheels of history are progressing. The author of today is no longer the author of thirteen or fourteen years ago, however, what has been destroyed by the wheels of history is not just the author alone...

After reading a part of "Zhou Zuoren's Letters" (Beixin edition), I felt a lot and picked up my pen to write this "trivial note." I wonder what other people who read this book will think.

Pearl S. Buck, Author of "The Good Earth" 222

— Yixian

Ms. Pearl S. Buck, whose Chinese name is Wen Xiang, is from Virginia, USA. She was only four months old when her parents brought her to China. Her father, Dr. Sai Zhaoxiang (Absalom Sydenstricker), was a Presbyterian missionary who preached in Qingjiang, Zhenjiang, and other places. He wrote many religious books and translated part of the New Testament. In his later years, he was a professor of theology at Jinling University in Nanjing. In the summer of 1931, he died of dysentery in Lushan, at the age of eighty. Her mother was also a missionary, and was very accomplished in literature, art, and music. She died early.

When Ms. Buck was young, she lived with her parents in a quiet cottage on a small hill near the county seat of Qingjiang. Her playmates, besides her sister, were all local Chinese children. She received her preliminary education from her mother. According to Ms. Buck's interview with a reporter from the New York Times, her mother "not only taught her the general curriculum of elementary school, but also gave her an appreciation for art and music, and, more importantly, made her aware of the pleasure of words themselves."

Because her missionary mother had many Chinese friends, Ms. Buck often went in and out of Chinese homes. She not only became familiar with Chinese customs, but also understood the inner pain of the Chinese working masses and housewives. She also had an old nanny who often told her stories of her childhood, famine, and bandits while sitting and mending socks or doing something else, giving her a deep impression. She lived among the Chinese in this way from childhood, so when she later came to study in schools in Shanghai, she hardly felt any difference between herself and the Chinese.

At the age of seventeen, Ms. Buck returned to the United States via Europe and studied at Randolph-Macon Woman's College in Virginia. She graduated with particularly good literary results and won the highest prize, a beautiful sofa. This sofa is still displayed in her living room. She came to China for the second time and successively served as a professor at Jinling University and Southeast University. In her spare time, she often wrote articles about the state of Chinese society and submitted them to major American magazines such as The Atlantic Monthly, The Nation, and Asia. Over time, Americans recognized her as a "China expert." (To be continued)

Ordinary Matters (27) 223

— Dan Guosun

"If you want to push it further, then you can only take the bills of lading for the materials in the foreign warehouses and mortgage them to foreign firms. This might get you about ten thousand [dollars]; besides that, the only thing left is the six or seven trucks in the factory, which can be mortgaged for three to five thousand. As for the materials currently in the factory, they don't amount to anything worth mentioning, so I don't need to talk about them. Zhi Guang, isn't this a general ledger of my personal financial resources! Do you think I've missed anything?"

"I don't think so!"

What did Zhi Guang think? What he felt was the failure of his plan. The hardship in Zhabei was truly as he had witnessed, proving that what he had previously heard was not exaggerated. Given the relationship between the two of them and Bo Tang's vision and financial resources, he thought he could persuade him to do something conscientious in Zhabei, but just now, from this general ledger, it was proven that Bo Tang's financial resources were not as abundant as he had previously thought. Of course, material deficiencies are difficult to ignore by finding stimulants! As for Bo Tang, his posture had changed at this time. He pulled his legs up and stepped on the chair, put his hands on his knees, and raised his head to stare at the wall opposite him. Thus, the straight bridge of his nose, which hung on his snow-white, slender face, now took on a horizontal position, just like the bow of a Norwegian three-masted warship. He had fallen into a state of contemplation, a battlefield in his own heart. He firmly believed that Zhi Guang's inspection and report in Zhabei were valuable, and he also believed that the limitations of his own financial resources were very obvious. What he was asking for now was a way to provide assistance that would please everyone, comfort himself, and not cause him trouble in the future. This method was certainly very carefully considered. He weighed it lightly and heavily in his heart, and his straight, ship-bow-like nose swayed left and right with his head; however, Zhi Guang did not realize this, so when he felt that the plan had failed and there was no way to implement it, he suddenly sighed deeply. Who knew that this immediately caused Bo Tang to let out a long sigh as well. Then Bo Tang asked:

"Zhi Guang, which point are you emphasizing with your sigh?"

"Emphasizing?" Zhi Guang said, "Why did I sigh... Perhaps it was because your financial resources have encountered such limitations!... Then, why are you sighing? Which point are you emphasizing?"

"My sigh is to blame myself for not having the courage to go to Zhabei to see for myself sooner! So now I don't have the courage to find a suitable way to provide assistance.... So I really want to go and see for myself tomorrow morning; this is not to do an investigation of your words; the purpose is entirely to arouse my own courage!"

Financial Foreign Exchange Fuels Gold Price Surge 224

丨Continued Rise of Eleven Dollars, One Dime丨

The gold market rose quite vigorously yesterday, the foreign exchange market was in a state of emergency, making buyers more emboldened. In the early morning, although the British pound rose, the US dollar fell by one dime. Although the forward silver price on the Gold Exchange fell by eight and a half厘, it had rebounded a lot from the previous day, so it had little impact. Stocks fell by a strong dollar. This Month's Yarn and Cotton 交割 (Settlement) Summary 232

5,100 Bales of Yarn and 18,900 Loads of Cotton

The July yarn contract was auctioned on February 1st, with a price of 145 taels and 9 mace, equivalent to approximately 204 yuan in foreign currency. Subsequently, spring sales stagnated, external threats in North China intensified daily, credit became extremely tight, rural areas in the interior declined, purchasing power was greatly diminished, sales became sluggish, yarn inventories accumulated, and manufacturers faced difficulties and significant losses. To maintain the survival of the factories, a meeting of the trade was convened in mid-April to shorten working hours and reduce production, resolving to halt operations for two half-days each week. This caused a slight shock to sentiment, and the market showed a slight rebound, but sales remained poor and the market struggled to improve. Midway through the month, the United States implemented a policy of currency inflation, causing U.S. cotton prices to rise, which lent some support to the market. However, prices fluctuated around 190 yuan, and yarn inventories continued to grow. By the middle of this month, sellers had ample supplies for delivery, but there was a significant lack of buyers for the old cotton yarn offered. Market sentiment was weak again. Later, a certain manufacturer purchased 1,200 bales in preparation for delivery, providing some support. The final transaction price was 184 yuan and 8 jiao, 3 yuan and 2 jiao lower than the June price. The resulting price difference for the three days of 交割 (settlement) was 186 yuan, with a total 交割 (settlement) volume of 5,100 bales. However, only 200 bales of 20-count cotton yarn were actually delivered; the rest was settled by themselves. The broker numbers and bales of the delivering and receiving parties are listed below:

The July Zhengzhou cotton contract was auctioned on February 1st, with a price of 33 taels, equivalent to approximately 46 yuan and 1.2 jiao in foreign currency. Subsequently, due to the weakness of Indian cotton and the stagnation of yarn sales, sentiment softened, and the market trended downward. Furthermore, there was much talk about yarn factories reducing work hours due to the poor yarn market. The lowest price seen was 41 yuan and 7 or 8 jiao. However, the U.S. government implemented a currency inflation plan, and U.S. cotton prices rose daily, driving up the cotton market. Later, in mid-May, competition between Britain and Japan for cotton intensified. In retaliation, Japan refused to purchase Indian cotton and switched to buying Chinese cotton instead. As a result, Japanese merchants extensively scoured Shandong, Zhengzhou, Tianjin, and other places. Shanghai was greatly shaken. Speculators, in conjunction with foreign merchants, purchased in the futures market, and calls for a short squeeze were loud and clear. Buyers were ambitious, anticipating 交割 (settlement) prices as high as 52 yuan. By the middle of this month, the highest price seen was 49 yuan and 3 jiao. Unexpectedly, U.S. cotton prices plummeted, and factories had ample supplies for delivery. Moreover, many yarn factories were suspending or reducing work hours. In the final days, those who had taken long positions, fearing the negative sentiment, rushed to close out their positions, and the price fell back to 47 yuan and 9 jiao. In the final transaction, a certain speculator surnamed Wang alone received over 10,000 loads of cotton. The price was 48 yuan and 6 jiao. As a result, the remaining 18,900 loads of goods, including Lingdou cotton, 火機 cotton, and Shaanxi cotton, were all 交割 (settled). The broker numbers and amount of each side are as follows:

Flour and Wheat Are Both Affected by Falling Foreign Wheat Prices 236

The wheat market is being pulled down by the falling prices of foreign wheat, with American wheat falling 1 yuan and 6 jiao and a half, and Canadian wheat falling 2 yuan and 2, 3 or 4 jiao. Coupled with the sluggish flour sales, the market naturally trends towards softness. However, profitable shortsellers are seizing the opportunity to cover their positions, so the market, while falling, is actually stable, with each month only falling 3 or 4 fen. This is the reason why. Until the afternoon opening, due to the shortsellers of brokers, they were again urgently covering their positions step by step. Interior customers are still unwilling to cut their losses, resulting in the market being buoyant instead, with fewer sellers. Each month rebounded by 2, 3 or 4 fen. However, this resurgence is only a fleeting glimmer, and the future is likely fraught with danger. As a result, August rose 2 fen, October remained down 1 fen, and the rest were unchanged. Currently, both cargo from customers and goods managed by brokers themselves arrive daily in the wheat market, with 江北貨 accounting for the majority.阜豐 has no appetite, and only 福新 is making slight arrangements. Therefore, the situation is deteriorating daily, and each grade has been cut short by 3 to 5 fen. 窰 wheat opens at 3 yuan and 7 jiao and 2 fen, Gaoyou wheat at 3 yuan and 6 jiao and 6 fen, second grade at 6 jiao and 3 fen, Zhenjiang wheat at 3 yuan and 5 jiao and a half, second grade at 5 jiao and 2 fen, Liuhe wheat at 3 yuan and 6 jiao and 3 fen, and Qingjiangpu wheat at 3 yuan and 6 jiao and 2 fen, totaling over 11,000 packages, reportedly managed by 福新.

After the flour market opened this year, there was a significant disturbance. Due to the fall in foreign wheat prices and the rumor that American wheat would be dumped in the East, the domestic flour sales are currently in a slump. The spread of this rumor has shaken the market. This month, the lowest price fell to 2 yuan and 2 jiao and 9 fen, August to 2 yuan and 3 jiao and 5 li, and September to 2 yuan and 3 jiao and a half, down 2, 3 or 4 fen from the previous day's closing price. After entering each transaction, due to major factories resisting the advance of this month, distant months were gradually sold short. The other factories also sold off smoothly, estimated to be over 500,000 packages. However, speculators from outside the industry seized the opportunity to cover their short positions, which was also very active. Therefore, the recent situation has rebounded by about 2 fen compared to the lowest point. However, sentiment for distant months is gradually softening due to the difficulty of seeing any improvement in the domestic sales market and the worry about the dumping of foreign wheat. As a result, compared to the previous day, it fell 1 fen and 2 li and a half, August fell 1 fen, September fell 1 fen and 7 li and a half, October fell 1 fen, November fell 1 fen, and December fell 1 fen and a half.

What is Our Future? 240

Recently, Japanese Minister of War Araki said in a speech somewhere: "Around 1936, the Yamato nation will face its most severe situation 丨I will fully prepare the people of our country with the spirit of Bushido to face this situation in the future." According to the Associated Press, Washington, 27th: "The U.S. Department of the Interior today paid the Army Department USD 6 million as part of the cost of improving national defense plans to build port defenses in the Panama Canal area and the Hawaiian Islands." It is heard that this is only part of the total national defense expenditure, and the entire amount is said to exceed USD 50 million. In addition, the United Kingdom, the United States, and Japan are also vigorously building warships at the same time to seize naval hegemony, and European countries are also using national defense as an excuse to expand their military preparations. If we recall the situation of the arms race between various countries before 1914, the world today is actually similar to the situation immediately before the European War, except that the area of conflict in the future will be in the Far East, not on the European continent. Under this severe situation, how should China prepare to cope with this unprecedented crisis? Based on our current situation, if we infer its future, it can only make people have a great deal of doubt and fear!

Today, any Chinese person should be deeply aware that China's future is our own future. If we have a little courage not to give up on ourselves, we must quickly plan the path of struggle and the strategies to cope with it. We must not think that the time in "1936" is still far away. We should know that the days of two or three years will come in an instant. Speaking realistically, if the Second World War really breaks out in "1936", then we will be able to prepare immediately, and I am afraid it will be too late, let alone prepare fundamentally? We imagine the inevitable tragic slaughter after the outbreak of the war, which will create an unprecedented new record in the history of killing people. If we immediately plan to prepare, then although there is a worry of being too late, it is always much better than being slaughtered on the spot. So, will our future be at the mercy of others, slaughtered, or will we have to fight a bloody path to continue to survive? This depends on our self-determination. Relying on苟安, hoping for luck, are all like dreaming!

Literary Arts for Store Employees

Uncle's Sorrow 242

--- Zhang Yu

Because of the bankruptcy of the rural economy, I reluctantly abandoned my lovely hometown and came to the city to work like an animal to get a little reward to make a living. But the situation in my hometown often lingers in my mind.

"Uncle is back!" This kind of cry from my nephews and nieces is what I always hear when I step onto the corner of the yard every time I go home. At the same time, my mother leans on the door, showing a kind smile, watching her grandchildren scramble to take my bag. Because every time I go home, I always bring them some candy cane or toys to eat or play with. Even if I don't buy it, my brother will ask me to bring some for them. They compete with each other to take my bag, half to welcome me home, but half also to get more candy canes and toys.

However, this time when I went home, although there was no change in other situations, the uncle's voice in the mouths of my nephews and nieces seemed a little harsh, and the smile on my mother's face was a little unnatural, and there were a few more crystal tears in her eyes. It turned out that my brother had died of illness last winter! So when she saw me, she thought of my brother's death, and therefore she was deeply saddened.

Every time I go home, I always bring back my brother's letter, or he asks me to bring her things that my mother likes and delicious food for her to enjoy. But, now? Although I also bring a little, but because of the oppression of the economy, after all, there is not as much as my brother used to ask me to bring!

Lifestyle

The Oriental Gambling City 243

--- Wang Mingxin

The Big Casino

At three o'clock in the night, Lao Wu, Xiao Wang and I went to a big casino to play. As soon as we entered the gate, our eyes lit up, and five hundred incandescent electric lights illuminated the entire flower garden. As soon as the car stopped, a gentlemanly receptionist ran over. When he saw us, he retreated, probably knowing that we no longer needed a "greeter."

After handing over our top hats and scarves to the waiter, he gave us three red gold watch pendants with two English floral letters on them. The first room we entered was a bank-like room, and the gilded railings and props made people's eyes feel uncomfortable. Because we didn't bring enough cash, we signed checks there. I exchanged a total of forty one-hundred-yuan chips. (For bets of less than one hundred yuan, cash should be used)

Walking through four or five rooms, mahjong, digging flowers, poker, pai gow, dice, shaking stands, everything was available. Of course, mahjong, digging flowers, and poker are too much trouble, so we just casually placed a few pai gow bets. Looking at the table, each pai entered and exited with more than 20,000 chips, with each bet averaging 1,000 yuan.

The most gamblers were in the dice and big roulette areas, and the number of bets placed there was also relatively small. Sometimes a small amount of cash could also be seen.

People who come here are indeed much more generous. They are very calm even when they earn one or two thousand, and they never show the joy of "the poor getting rich." Even if they lose 100,000 or 80,000, they dare to be calm and composed, without the slightest smile, and never look "vicious and evil" like in other casinos. This big casino covers an area of ​​about dozens of acres, with the flower garden accounting for most of it, and half of the four-story western-style building with ten floors and ten bottoms is empty. Only when you come to this casino can you see what is really called gambling, which is beyond the reach of other casinos; if you compare the Jai Alai court and the dog racing court with this place, it is even more ridiculous and simple.

Most of the gamblers are sea-dwelling gentry and children of wealthy gentry. Their extravagant demeanor and gorgeous clothes are probably unimaginable to the average person. If you eavesdrop on us calculating the gambling accounts, you will definitely think that what we are talking about may be the number of "paper marks." In fact, the amazing huge amount of ins and outs are regarded as very normal here.

Because the indoor air was not very good, we went outside for a walk. There were at least 500 vehicles lined up outside, but because the gamblers were scattered everywhere, it didn't feel crowded. A young lady dressed as a thousand gold handed over three cotton-headed French cigarettes. After lighting them, Xiao Wang casually gave her two ten-yuan bills. In addition, the price of three cups of coffee and tea, western desserts, fruit sundaes, and three towels was half a hundred yuan. In fact, these are all freely available to customers without taking a penny, and what you pay is just the money for the rouge and powder on those jade hands.

The room was full of the scent of Parisian perfume, too strong. For people who are not used to it, it can simply cause a headache. The futuristic props (which did not exist in the 181 era) made the average gambler feel like they were on a stage or screen, and the waiter's eagerness made us feel like "Ford Kings." After gambling for a long time, I was really a little bored, so I forcibly pulled Lao Wu and Xiao Wang out.

When we returned to the place where we exchanged chips, they looked at my chips and said, "9,500 cash!" Really, they had a lot of cash, and amounts less than 10,000 were not paid by check. I was already tired and only placed a few bets. I won some and lost some, and I didn't know when I exchanged five one-thousand-yuan tokens. But Xiao Wang and Lao Wu were unlucky that day and each lost several thousand yuan.

We took back our hats and scarves, and paid 20 yuan in small accounts before walking out inexplicably. At this time, the gambling

Page 20

The gamblers have already left one-third, and there are two new "Lincoln cars" waiting at the door besides my car, with the doors open. Xiao Wang and Lao Wu each got into one. I knew that this was specially used by the big casino to send off guests, and nominally it was free, but I was afraid that each of them would have to spend a small sum on a banquet.

My car was halfway there, and the customs bell was already ringing at eight o'clock. So I asked the driver to take me directly to the office, because there was nothing important waiting for me to deal with there, and there was comfortable bedding prepared for me there.

The driver told me very happily that it was more than a night's salary. I smiled, and he said, "The people in the room said, please tell your master to come often in the future! I will tell you!"

Dancing Hall: Forest of Legs and Meat 244

— Yang Moyun

A dance hostess is the soul of a dancing hall. Truly, if a dancing hall doesn't have a few dance hostesses who can get by, it's better to close down shop sooner rather than later.

In order to increase their sexual appeal, they sometimes don't hesitate to sacrifice their modesty and don't even wear stockings, exposing their thighs all the way up (their shorts are so short they only cover their private parts). Oh, those thighs! I don't know how many men have drowned in them! But even if every young man on the entire planet died out completely, they probably wouldn't bat an eye, and would immediately turn around and attack those dying old men. They only recognize shiny silver dollars! Other than that, their eyes are covered with tinted glass...

Some of them already have husbands, some already have "trailers" (a nickname for lovers, meaning "concubines"), and even more have lost their freedom like prostitutes. So, those "suckers" freely order champagne and give away dance tickets, which to them are just unexpected windfalls. They once said sweet words, feigned shyness or anger, using extremely seductive glances, and even sacrificing a kiss, but as soon as they leave you, they'll go and treat someone else like that. To say something disappointing, all the "sucker money" they get from you is given to their husbands or "trailers." What's more, what will make you feel like "Am I being treated like a fool?" is that when they go home at dawn, they've already forgotten about you, and are instead snuggling their snow-white bodies in the arms of their husbands or "trailers," pursuing playful love and sexual revelry...

However, these poor dance hostesses, dancing with customers from nine o'clock every night until three or four in the morning, their legs and feet are made of flesh and blood, not iron. They have tired legs, aching legs, and they go home with aching legs. Why do those young masters who treat dance hostesses as playthings only know how to buy smiles with money, and don't know how to soothe their pain?

X X X X X

But if a dancing hall relies solely on a few dance tickets to survive, the dancing hall owner's wife will definitely not be few in number; otherwise, if there's only one wife, it won't be enough to cover the losses. Of course, dance hostesses are the soul of a dancing hall; even a dance customer who goes to a dancing hall to dance has to do some investigation before going to a dancing hall that he thinks has the most beautiful dance hostesses. However, although the owner hopes that all his dance hostesses are as beautiful as heavenly goddesses, he doesn't want to earn money solely from a few dance tickets, because for every hundred dollars of dance tickets sold, he only gets fifty dollars in hand; and he still has to provide food and drink for the dance hostesses, and he has to spend money to print the dance tickets. What he hopes for is that more wine is sold, and he doesn't mind selling more tea, coffee, cocoa, soda, and elaborate white dishes, etc. For example, a bottle of brandy costs ten dollars, but sold cup by cup, it can sell for at least forty dollars; coffee, tea, cocoa, and soda cost five cents per cup or bottle. Look, drinking a cup of tea or a bottle of soda for five cents, even the emperor who considers himself the only one worthy doesn't drink anything better? (If you treat a dance hostess to a cocktail, to be honest, it's not a glass of wine, but a glass of cold tea - four-fifths is tea, and only one-fifth is wine - and the price is two cents more; these two cents are given to the dance hostess, perhaps as a bonus.)

So the Bar (wine and soda, etc. belong to the Bar) and the Kitchen (tea, coffee, elaborate white dishes, etc. belong to the Kitchen) are the two cash cows of a dancing hall. X X X X X

In addition to the monthly rent, which is a major expense, the musicians' salaries are also considerable. The salaries of a band of American musicians are at least three thousand dollars per month; a band of Filipino musicians also gets about two thousand dollars; even the cheapest Russian musicians can't do without a thousand dollars per band. Paid every half month, if there's no money when the time comes, they'll use force. If you often treat them to champagne, or give them an extra bottle of beer to drink, they can get the customers to spend more money - shortening the time for playing music and resting, while increasing the number of times they play music, so the sales of dance tickets will be better.

As for the European servants, they are very ruthless. "Red eyes, green eyebrows," if you're not careful, they'll rip you off while you're dazed by wine and women.

Other things, such as cigarettes and candies, etc., are priced one or two times higher than outside, which is already known to everyone, and I don't need to repeat it. As for one dollar only being worth ten cents (small silver coins), that's an open secret, but only the rich go to dancing halls, and they certainly won't haggle over one or two cents; this is considered a bargain for the accountant.

X X X X X

In short, a dancing hall is a book with a beautifully decorated cover, but if you open its table of contents, the entire content it contains is just: bitter wine, skulls, walking corpses, living dead, a den of demons, sorrow and joy, a demonic dance, the burial of youth... A cozy nest? A dark shop.

White knives go in, red knives come out, intimidation, deception, the law of the jungle, the crossroads of life and death, the opposition of rich and poor, the sale of flesh, the labor of legs, the pouring of music, the stimulation of tobacco and alcohol, loving beauty but not the country... These, these, are interwoven into a dancing hall.

Special Self-Employment Introduction

I Need Work and Bread 245

— Ms. Meiwei

The Buddhist scriptures say: "If there is no birth, then there is no death," then my flesh and blood are being wasted in struggling for this miserable "life"! When I see withered and frightening faces, my heart can't help but cry out! From the fluttering snowflakes to the scorching sun, these months of unemployment are like being kicked into a bottomless abyss, like being thrown into a trap where you can't live or die. My distraught mind makes me like a homeless dog! Unable to go up to heaven, unable to go down to earth, a homeless dog lost in the east, west, south, and north!

The embarrassing situation of a homeless, wandering person like me when they become unemployed is probably something that successful people can't even imagine! Especially in this cold and fickle world, without money or power, people like me who are lonely are annoying enough to relatives and friends when they accidentally see them, let alone inquire about them. I remember Lu Xun said, "Those who have fallen from a well-off family into poverty, those who have come through this journey have seen through the true face of the world." How true are these words about the ways of the world! Truly, I am a person who has tasted all the cold shoulders on the road of life!

The practical problem, "life," still oppresses me very seriously, but what else can this lost person do besides hold a wounded and painful heart and shake their brain with disappointment all day long! Whenever I wake up in the middle of the night, the horror of unemployment makes me ask myself in shock: "If this kind of life continues..." Alas! This stumps me! These six months, hiding in a small attic less than five feet wide, have been as blurry as a dream, and I don't even know how I got through them. Sometimes I unconsciously wander aimlessly on the road. In this city with alternating red and green lights, how desolate and bewildered is the heart of a lonely, unemployed person when they see those people with fat heads and big faces, flying with excitement? Ah! Who would have thought that the sea of life would be so uneven? I look up at the sky and down at the earth, and my mind is blank!

At this time, I think of Shelley wandering in a foreign land and Qu Yuan with grief filling his chest, wandering by the Luo River and eventually sinking into the vast waves. I think of how they could still write brilliant elegies! But what about me? ... These chaotic thoughts flood my mind; two weak legs accompany a thin shadow, and when I return to the dormitory entrance, I hear the landlady and her daughter laughing and talking. Suddenly, it hangs heavy in the heart of a wanderer who has fallen to the ends of the earth! It's like a big stone, instantly becoming heavy!

Ten years ago, I had already been driven by hunger and cold to leave my hometown and embark on the road of life. Although I don't have a special skill, I have never received any help in the past ten years. I have always found my own bread and struggled on the road of fierce survival competition. In the past, I have worked as a teacher in primary and secondary schools, a tutor, and other similar jobs. Now I sincerely want to sell my labor. If readers of this newspaper have a place where I can be of use, no matter how big or small the task, I am willing to serve as a maid. My request dares not be great. Although I have lived for thirty-two years, I still do not have a family or other places that I have to bear. I only need to be able to maintain my own minimum standard of living. Correspondence can be forwarded through this publication.

Mysterious Building 246

— Song Chuping

General Assembly

This is the XX Senior Club of the Great Republic of China. Although it is located on XX Road, a road built across the border in the suburbs of Shanghai, the location is very quiet. Every night from 9:00 PM to 3:00 or 4:00 AM, club members can drive their cars at will without the trouble of running over people.

In this towering three-dimensional building of the club, no one knows how many rooms there are, except for the superintendent of the house and the engineer who made the blueprints. Each floor and each room has very ingenious and secret facilities, so that people can discuss important matters. There are also card rooms, smoking rooms, mahjong, poker, kowtow, chess sets, music... Each part has extremely valuable and precious items, and various different beautifying decorations. The electric lights emit a gentle and charming glow, reflecting the faces of adult gentlemen with their joys, sorrows, angers, and pleasures, fat and thin, yellow and white. The waiters carefully and attentively listen to and accept the commands and instructions of anyone. The thick, soft carpet heavily bears the trampling and pounding of leather shoes and canes. The exquisitely embroidered silk cushions often receive large, dignified buttocks and the ash of cigar licks. When the silk flower tablecloth is stained with coffee, tea, or colored iced drink water stains, the waiters are very accustomed to immediately replacing it with another clean tablecloth. Air-conditioning pipes and water tinges replace unregulated electric fans or electric stoves, and unsuitable excessively cold or excessively hot weather can be arbitrarily controlled in winter and summer. Some of the cards are like jade and some are like opaque crystal, with emerald green or pink tough backs, and after rubbing against the table for several hours, the waiters have at least two or three hundred dollars of income, not to mention that the four warriors have tens of thousands of dollars of winnings and losses. Those who have had enough of the addiction, leisurely holding rolls of banknotes of fifty dollars or more, or the club's special chips, often stand behind the mahjong game to observe the situation and place bets...

Yes, everything seems leisurely and extravagant.

However, the deliberation of national economic, political, and other important issues is often resolved here after cards and wine! Those who patronize this place are at least high officials and dignitaries or wealthy businessmen who can manipulate part of the power of society. In short, they are people of value! Their conversations and actions can maintain the safety of the entire society; they come here not hoping to enjoy any personal pleasure, but in addition to sitting, playing, eating, and drinking, there are many problems related to the lives of millions of people that need to be discussed and negotiated here!

In the dense shade of the trees, this six-story Western-style building built in 1932 is lying down. Those who have never been inside certainly do not know its wealth and greatness. It is already a very difficult thing to penetrate the tall glass windows with various window curtains in all seasons and see the ceiling inside. Who can imagine everything inside? And the noisy sounds of joy, card games, music, and conversations inside, of course, cannot penetrate outside. On the road with martial law, people only see an exhibition of rows of new cars and this mysterious building when passing by.

3,000,000 248

— Ji Xixi

Grand Theater

XXX Road, such a long XXX Road! The July sun is strangely fierce, and XXX Road is soft. These green, oily leaves shade the sidewalks; there are no girls strolling, no Pekingese running, it's strangely desolate. But, this place is noisy again!

It's across from XX Hall, under a great three-dimensional building, one after another, groups of "Citroens," "Dodges," "Lincolns," "......," are roaring.

Ah! The first grand theater in X City.

Today! I'm going to take the price I got from selling my blood, step into this crystallization of the public's blood and sweat, and enjoy the three million dollars worth of equipment.

Under the construction of marble, stepping on the ground of mica stone, how smooth! I'm holding this surprised heart, stepping with timid steps, slipping and slipping, slipping to the fountain, next to which are laid out many, many flowers and plants, and the water spraying out: crimson, dark green, azure, blue-green, ...... are interlaced.

It's still early, the doors inside haven't opened yet, but people are already crowded. Men, women; some are sitting on elastic sofas, some are pacing on the smooth mica stone: waiting, admiring the yellow patterned house.

Ah! These women of July, seductive women, are draped in these thin, cicada-wing-like "imported goods," and in the reflection of this yellow house, they look extraordinarily charming and extraordinarily seductive.

As the curtain opens, they rush in one after another, and the cold air fills my body. I'm dazed, I suspect I'm in the icebergs of the Arctic!

Having chosen a seat, looking back, the seats around me are full. Looking at the stage in front, under the shining crystal lights, the lake-green curtain is fluttering, and faint music is drifting out from here. On the patterned roof, the electric lights are mysteriously hidden inside. I feel the cold air lightly floating all over my body, how cool, how comfortable!

The whole theater is plunged into darkness, and all I can recognize clearly are John Barrymore and Dana Wynham on the screen.

But what about the owner who created this house? He's still creating under the scorching sun, never able to run inside again, under the supervision of the servants.

Film Special Issue

The Surrealism of "Scenery Problems in Chinese Films" 250

— Xu Xingzhi

After reading Mr. Miwu's "Scenery Problems in Chinese Films," it aroused many of my thoughts. The "first is the non-reality of the scenery" and "the second is the inability to unify the plot" proposed by Mr. Miwu are the biggest defects in Chinese film scenery at present.

But why are there these defects? According to my experience in the studio: (1) it is because the scenery designer lacks the experience of real life, and (2) it is because of the lack of communication between the director and the scenery designer.

In the studio, the director sometimes considers that a certain scene is beautiful and the cost is too expensive, and it seems a pity to shoot so few shots, so he adds some meaningless shots and plots. Conversely, because the scenery is not beautiful, the director thinks it will affect the ugliness of the picture, so he arbitrarily reduces the necessary performances and shots. In this way, because of the different scenery of the scenery designer, the director's original plan is often changed.

On the other hand, the scenery designer lacks the experience of real life and the knowledge of architectural decoration. Apart from buying some reference books from the bookstore and moving the foreign interior decoration and furnishings into Chinese films as a whole, he never considers the composition of Chinese real life. As a result, as Mr. Miwu said, "a rich man's home" is decorated with "extravagant and luxurious devices," and at the same time, "a salary-class home" is also "such a novel set."

Therefore, the scenery designer's scenery in the film not only affects the entire plot, but sometimes simply controls the director's thinking and the photographer's plan. Often the director changes the fixed directing plan because of the different scenery. Moreover, because of the richness and simplicity of the scenery, the unified mood of the play is broken. In this way, because of the surrealization of the scenery (partially), the entire plot (wholly) is affected by the surrealization.

In the studio, what is the situation of Chinese directors and scenery designers: On the first night, the director greets the scenery designer and says, "Tomorrow I want a good-looking coffee shop." However, because of time constraints, and even more because he does not understand the plot, the scenery designer casually chooses a picture from the book or writes a picture himself and gives it to the carpenter. The next day, the director sees the quality of the scenery and then makes plans. In this way, the director also becomes surreal, and then the entire film mechanism becomes surreal.

Here, in order to avoid these shortcomings, we require that the installation of film scenery is best designed by the director himself. If the director is not good at drawing and designing, he must at least give the scenery designer a general outline or model. At the same time, the scenery designer must also know the plot, characters, performances, and all the actions in the play; during shooting, the director and the photographer must constantly communicate in order to achieve a unified result. At least we still require that each director must have basic knowledge of drawing, architecture, and decorative arts.

Film Review

Review of "Westward Passage" 251

— Ling He

丨Dahua Ying丨

After watching this film, I think many people will be saddened by this plot. Especially the intellectuals of the middle class, perhaps even more will admit the literary success of this film. In fact, this is a novel adaptation. I personally know very little about the original author, but judging from the story of this film, it is not necessarily a naturalistic work. At the same time, the reason why the original author wants to use writers as the object of depiction may be that this kind of subject matter can better obtain his own deep experience. Writers are rich in emotions, unable to be rational in the face of events and prone to emotional actions, which should be the most common phenomenon of inferiority. In addition, when they are poor, the whip of life beats them, so troubled moods often cause violent actions. Moreover, the enjoyment of material things cannot give his wife even a low degree of satisfaction, so it is reasonable for poor couples to eventually break up. However, letting his wife take his daughter to remarry someone else is still a painful hidden pain. Under such circumstances, they meet again in a foreign land, the daughter calls her father, and the wife thinks of the former love, what is the feeling! Although they finally reconcile, this kind of hardship ultimately makes people feel deep sadness, especially the Story does not deviate from the economic foundation, which is a more correct understanding.

As mentioned above, the emotion of this film is indeed very successful. In particular, the director describes it very delicately, bit by bit, all are the expression of emotion. Especially after they reconciled, they went to the hotel where they had had extreme love, and quarreled again over trivial matters, and the wife decided to leave again, but stopped because she saw her daughter's toys; this simple technique is really rare. As for accidentally damaging her husband's manuscript and making him angry immediately, this is the original author's most profound brushstroke, and it is also the director's proud technique. However, on the whole, it is inevitably a bit dull, but if it is to maintain the mood of the original work, there is no way to do it. Moreover, it may still be very suitable for audiences with a little literary interest.

We don't know much about this director, Mr. Robert Milton, but even in this work alone, we cannot ignore the depth of his artistic cultivation. He not only has appropriate use of editing and editing, but also the configuration of music is very delicate, such as the final playing of Piana.

It is probably very suitable for Ann Harding to play the role of a virtuous wife, just like her previous roles of the same personality have not failed. Laurence Oliver's writer seems insufficient. Zasu Pitts is also very good here.

However, this film has a biggest shortcoming, which is the failure of sound recording. This loss is somewhat regrettable.

"Film Critic Personnel" in the Morning News Daily Film Section 252

The Morning News Daily Film, which has always condescended to offer "advice" or "contributions" to the Shanghai News film supplement, published a piece of "Film Critic Personnel" news yesterday. It wrote, "It is said that film critic Ling Hejun will be the editor of the Shanghai News film supplement. Last night at 10 o'clock, he gathered many film critics on Bubbling Well Road to discuss the organization of a film critic group. The details and results are unknown." We don't know where this news came from. The Daily Film has always been very keen to hear about the "personnel" of our newspaper; however, sometimes it makes jokes. For example, because it attacked A too fiercely, it deliberately added a couple of sentences praising B, when in fact A and B are the same person. The editor of this supplement has never exposed these things, letting them guess. Now this piece of "personnel" news is probably due to inaccurate measurement. As for whether there are other malicious intentions, as Ling Hejun himself suspects, I can't control much. Outsiders fabricating news to hurt feelings will certainly not be effective. As for the words "Bu Min" (Unskilled) signed by the current editor of this supplement, it is also a fictitious pen name. If Ling Hejun becomes the editor of the Shanghai News film supplement in the future, I will definitely offer him the old sign of "Bu Min."
