Review of "The Fighting Marshal" 253

— Wan Shi

Another martial arts film.

However, I always find it strange that, with the almost complete ban on domestic martial arts films in China, the United States still sends in this type of film in large quantities. Then it is no problem that this kind of work that caters to low-level interests can still be quite popular in China, otherwise why would it come in an endless stream? Perhaps foreign goods are much better than domestic products after all, and they do not harm

Chinese society; the reason why it is not banned lies in this.

However, in terms of this film, its content is not necessarily in line with the above conditions. Obviously, it is a work modeled after the "Tales of Jianghu Knights" and other works. A hero, in order to avenge the murder of his father, breaks out of prison, impersonates an official, abuses his power for personal gain, and single-handedly fights. At the same time, the hero must be amorous, and therefore holds a beauty in his arms. In the end, the father's revenge is avenged, the hero also submits to the law, and the good things are harmonized. Is there any educational significance in this? Is this a typical character? However, linking "revenge" and "submitting to the law" is very much in line with modern rules, so killing officials and impersonating officials does not make those in power frown.

I think it is not necessary to estimate the artistic value of this kind of film. Regardless of how sophisticated the film company's machinery is, regardless of how skilled the authors are, is it not a waste of money and energy to put a gorgeous coat on such a boring story? What's more, you can't turn a straw man into a living thing. Even if it looks like a person, it is still just scaring birds and beasts.

To put it more clearly, the performance techniques of this film are, in every respect, rudimentary, old-fashioned, vulgar, and superficial. Riding, running, escaping, chasing, mutually reflecting again and again, the result is winning vulgar applause and empty tension. If this is in line with the "time and space" theory in film theory, then what a ridiculous thing film will be! To put it bluntly, if we continue to work hard like this, film art will be going backwards and returning to the past.

Many people say that movies are not textbooks but purely entertainment. I don't want to explain whether this statement can be established here, but this kind of film cannot give us full entertainment, can it? I wonder if the readers who have seen this film feel the same way?

Recent State of American Theaters 254

— He Zui

In recent years, the business that can truly express the tendencies of American society is the abnormal development of urban entertainment facilities.

Since the end of the 19th century, when the entire economic organization of the United States leaned towards mechanical production, the working hours of the people have been shortening day by day, and people generally feel idle and their lives become monotonous; then, to receive enjoyment by the best method is the most appropriate, someone once advocated this, and hoped that this enjoyment must be popularized to the working masses. Sure enough, in the last twenty years, this ideal has gradually turned into a reality. The expansion of the film industry is a good example. According to a public survey in the United States, in January 1932, there were a total of 22,731 publicly operating movie theaters in the United States (excluding territories), which could accommodate 11.3 million viewers. If calculated at three shows a day, then 33.9 million people would visit theaters every day.

According to the statistics of 1931, the weekly audience also exceeded 100 million people, and the total amount of ticket sales was 150 million gold dollars.

As for the exact amount of investment in the film industry, although there are no accurate statistics, it must be around 200 million yuan. The amazing development of the American film industry can greatly express its modernized color.

Furthermore, in the United States these days, almost everything is in a recession. However, the theaters in New York are still so easy to attract people. Thinking about this, one can imagine it.

Pilgrimage to Film Studios in Europe and America (11) 255

— Yun Yan

Next to the Leixunda Film Studio is the distribution department of the Swiss Film Company. Many Swedish theaters are affiliated with it. One of the largest theaters has extremely attentive service. If movie fans in Stockholm want to book seats in that theater, they only need to pick up the phone and say "SFTickets" to talk to the theater's telephone operator. Not only can they book seats, but they can also

tell you the details of the weather.

(14) New Babylon City (Germany) Ncudabelsberg

丨Wufa Company Film Studio near Berlin丨

Among all the film studios in Europe, the Wufa City is the most complete and modern. It is located in New Babylon City near Berlin. It has fourteen separate sound stages and forty-two buildings for film production. But in 1912, there was only a small glass house there, used as a film studio, just to avoid the wind and rain. It was not until April 1929 that the new Wufa City was rebuilt. The circulation of air inside and outside the studio uses scientific methods. No matter how thunderous the sound is outside, it will not be transmitted to the eardrums of the staff in the studio.

The Wufa City factory uses 100,000 cubic yards of stacked wood and bamboo cloth, 40,000 cubic yards of paving boards, 600,000 feet of planks and moldings, 300 tons of plaster, 6,000 square feet of glass, and 1 million kilowatts of electricity every year. Surrounding the film studio are rows of modern dressing rooms, bathrooms, and lounges. There are also offices and dormitories for the 500 film studio partners. They produce 16 million feet of film every year.

In terms of machinery, there is nothing to criticize. Even in terms of human work, I am afraid that no film studio can match its spirit of cooperation. In a restaurant in the film studio, you will see electricians and temporary actresses sitting together for dinner, carpenters drinking coffee with cooks, and stars often discussing the difficulties in the film with the director there. They employ 800 workers, and everyone is very harmonious and cooperative. This is indeed a special strength of Wufa City. (The End)
